<p><span style="font-size: 10pt;">Table 7. List of files with their extensions that the stealer is looking for.</span></p>
<p>Additionally, the <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">CreateFileList</span> function searches for any files matching the name patterns of various cryptocurrency-related terms and names as shown in Figure 23.</p>
<figure id="attachment_143574" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-143574" style="width: 888px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img  class="wp-image-143574 lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/06/word-image-669052-143320-23.png" alt="Screenshot of a computer screen displaying a PowerShell script used for handling file management operations." width="888" height="399" data-srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/06/word-image-669052-143320-23.png 888w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/06/word-image-669052-143320-23-786x353.png 786w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/06/word-image-669052-143320-23-768x345.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 888px) 100vw, 888px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-143574" class="wp-caption-text">Figure 23. <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">CreateFileList</span> function as shown in <a href="https://code.visualstudio.com/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Visual Studio Code</a>.</figcaption></figure>
<p>All matching files are then written into a text file named <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">FileList.txt</span>.</p>
<p>The <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">RegisterTask</span> function shown in Figure 24 creates an entry in the Windows registry under <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Run</span> key for persistence. For this, it creates an entry named <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">WindowsSecurityCheck</span> and uses the file path to <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">1.vbs</span> previously dropped from the ZIP archive.</p>
<figure id="attachment_143585" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-143585" style="width: 884px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img  class="wp-image-143585 lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/06/word-image-671989-143320-24.png" alt="Screenshot of computer code using PowerShell functions, including commands such as &quot;RegisterTask.&quot;" width="884" height="113" data-srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/06/word-image-671989-143320-24.png 884w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/06/word-image-671989-143320-24-786x100.png 786w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/06/word-image-671989-143320-24-768x98.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 884px) 100vw, 884px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-143585" class="wp-caption-text">Figure 24. <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">RegisterTask</span> function as shown in <a href="https://code.visualstudio.com/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Visual Studio Code</a>.</figcaption></figure>
<p>A commented-out code line in <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">1.ps1</span> (see Figure 24, line 409) indicates it has run <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">1.log</span> directly in the malware code at some point. This functionality has been outsourced to the external file <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">1.vbs</span>, which contains VBScript code obfuscated by the same algorithm as for all other files. Figure 25 below shows its deobfuscated version.</p>
<figure id="attachment_143596" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-143596" style="width: 737px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img  class="wp-image-143596 lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/06/word-image-674985-143320-25.png" alt="Screenshot of a Visual Studio Code interface showing a section of JavaScript code to create an object named WScript.shell." width="737" height="80" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-143596" class="wp-caption-text">Figure 25. VBScript code of <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">1.vbs</span> as shown in <a href="https://code.visualstudio.com/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Visual Studio Code</a>.</figcaption></figure>
<p>The last function <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">Work</span> continuously interacts with the C2 server, cycling through a set of operations as shown in Figure 26. This function is similar to the procedure of the PE variant. It periodically uploads the collected data and provides the attacker with backdoor functionality. This includes uploading any additional files to the C2 server or downloading and running additional PowerShell payloads to the victim’s system.</p>
<figure id="attachment_143607" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-143607" style="width: 487px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img  class="wp-image-143607 lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/06/word-image-677958-143320-26.png" alt="Screenshot of a computer script in a programming interface for the function Work, including function definitions and commands primarily related to web operations. The syntax is highlighted for readability." width="487" height="434" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-143607" class="wp-caption-text">Figure 26. Excerpt of the <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">Work</span> function as shown in <a href="https://code.visualstudio.com/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Visual Studio Code</a>.</figcaption></figure>
<p>The control flow is as follows:</p>
<ol>
<li>The function is initiated by pausing for 600 seconds.</li>
<li>It then constructs a URL <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;"><em>&lt;C2URL&gt;</em>?id=<em>&lt;UUID&gt;</em>&amp;ap=1</span> to upload a file named <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">k.log</span> to the C2 server. The keylogger module creates this file.</li>
<li>After the upload, the function deletes the file <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">k.log</span> from the local machine.</li>
<li>It downloads a string from a server URL <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;"><em>&lt;C2URL&gt;</em>?id/rd</span> and splits it into lines. For each line, which is a provided file path, it constructs a URL <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;"><em>&lt;C2URL&gt;</em>?id=<em>&lt;UUID&gt;</em></span> and uploads the file to the server. Afterwards, it sends a GET request to a URL <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;"><em>&lt;C2URL&gt;</em>?id=<em>&lt;UUID&gt;</em>&amp;del=rd</span> to delete the read string from the server.</li>
<li>Next, it downloads a string from another server URL <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;"><em>&lt;C2URL&gt;</em>?id/wr</span> and splits it into lines. For each line, it extracts the filename, constructs a URL <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;"><em>&lt;C2URL&gt;</em>?id=<em>&lt;UUID&gt;</em>/<em>&lt;FileName&gt;</em></span> and downloads this file from the server to the victim’s system. It then sends a GET request to a URL <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;"><em>&lt;C2URL&gt;</em>?id=<em>&lt;UUID&gt;</em>&amp;del=<em>&lt;FileName&gt;</em></span> to delete the file from the server.</li>
<li>It downloads a string from a C2 server URL <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;"><em>&lt;C2URL&gt;</em>?id/cm</span> and executes the string as a command using <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">Invoke-Expression</span>. This string can be any PowerShell code but is likely used to run additional payloads dropped previously. After execution, it sends a GET request to a URL <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;"><em>&lt;C2URL&gt;</em>?id=<em>&lt;UUID&gt;</em>&amp;del=cm</span> to delete the string on the server.</li>
<li>The function repeats this entire process indefinitely.</li>
</ol>
<p>During our analysis of this malware, we did not observe any data returned from the C2 server.</p>
<p>The last of the three parts of the stealer’s code is the main function logic shown in Figure 27.</p>
<figure id="attachment_143618" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-143618" style="width: 793px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img  class="wp-image-143618 lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/06/word-image-680929-143320-27.png" alt="A screenshot of a computer script in a text editor, including various command lines and a PowerShell command, which is prominent in the display. The script includes tasks like registering a task, initiating and getting browser data. " width="793" height="145" data-srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/06/word-image-680929-143320-27.png 793w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/06/word-image-680929-143320-27-786x144.png 786w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/06/word-image-680929-143320-27-768x140.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 793px) 100vw, 793px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-143618" class="wp-caption-text">Figure 27. Main function logic as shown in <a href="https://code.visualstudio.com/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Visual Studio Code</a>.</figcaption></figure>
<p>First, this section creates the malware persistence in the registry and then collects system information and browser data. Next, it runs the file <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">2.log</span> using the PowerShell loader script <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">1.ps1</span> before it finally sends all data to the C2 server and waits for the attacker’s commands.</p>
<p>The file <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">2.log</span> is a keylogger module that captures and records keystrokes, window titles and clipboard content as shown in Figure 28. This module writes the recorded data into a log file named <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">k.log</span>, which is uploaded to the C2 server in the <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">Work</span> function.</p>
<figure id="attachment_143629" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-143629" style="width: 799px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img  class="wp-image-143629 lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/06/word-image-683896-143320-28.png" alt="Screenshot of a computer script displayed in a text editor with dark background, showing several lines of code written in PowerShell for the Keylog function. The code involves functions related to capturing and managing keyboard input." width="799" height="352" data-srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/06/word-image-683896-143320-28.png 799w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/06/word-image-683896-143320-28-786x346.png 786w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/06/word-image-683896-143320-28-768x338.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 799px) 100vw, 799px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-143629" class="wp-caption-text">Figure 28. Base64-decoded keylogger code of <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">2.log</span> as shown in <a href="https://code.visualstudio.com/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Visual Studio Code</a>.</figcaption></figure>
<h2><a id="post-143320-_6sn1o7quy58s"></a>Previous Version of KimJongRAT PowerShell Variant</h2>
<p>We’ve found a previous version of the PowerShell variant that only differs slightly from the most recent one. The main differences are in the PowerShell script in the stealer.</p>
<p>The <a href="https://www.virustotal.com/gui/file/28f2fcece68822c38e72310c911ef007f8bd8fd711f2080844f666b7f371e9e1" target="_blank" rel="noopener">initial LNK file</a> downloads an HTA file named <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">prevenue.hta</span> from an attacker-controlled <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">cdn.glitch[.]global</span> URL. The URL to the HTA file contains the value <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">1742020326408</span> for the parameter <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">v</span>. This value is the time in epoch format for <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">Saturday, March 15, 2025, 6:32 a.m.</span> (GMT). The LNK file’s metadata is identical to the one used in the most recent version.</p>
<p>The <a href="https://www.virustotal.com/gui/file/3c2ea04090ad8c28116c42a9a2be5b240f135ac184e5a2c121b4eb311a7bf075" target="_blank" rel="noopener">downloaded HTA file</a> named <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">prevenue.hta</span> is almost identical to the HTA file used in the most recent version. The only differences are the <a href="https://www.virustotal.com/gui/file/48fc82c91f86fe783f9c0e2ec46f5b48aae3fd08c94342576eb194b0c9bb1de6" target="_blank" rel="noopener">embedded decoy PDF file</a> dropped as <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">revenue.pdf</span> and the embedded ZIP archive containing a previous version of the PowerShell stealer.</p>
<p>The decoy PDF file shown in Figure 29 seems to be a tax revenue-related document of a person from the South Korean city of Sejong.</p>
<figure id="attachment_143640" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-143640" style="width: 679px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img  class="wp-image-143640 lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/06/word-image-686970-143320-29.png" alt="Image shows a form featuring various sections with personal details, registration number, and a QR code, all displayed in Korean characters." width="679" height="743" data-srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/06/word-image-686970-143320-29.png 679w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/06/word-image-686970-143320-29-402x440.png 402w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/06/word-image-686970-143320-29-640x700.png 640w" sizes="(max-width: 679px) 100vw, 679px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-143640" class="wp-caption-text">Figure 29. PDF decoy document <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">revenue.pdf</span> as shown in <a href="https://www.adobe.com/acrobat/pdf-reader.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Adobe PDF Reader</a>.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Figure 30 shows the contents of the ZIP archive again dropped as <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">pipe.zip</span>.</p>
<figure id="attachment_143651" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-143651" style="width: 759px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img  class="wp-image-143651 lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/06/word-image-690347-143320-30.png" alt="A screenshot showing a list of four files in a file explorer, detailing their size, packed size, modified, created, and accessed dates, as well as attributes. " width="759" height="100" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-143651" class="wp-caption-text">Figure 30. Files contained in <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">pipe.zip</span> as shown in <a href="https://www.7-zip.org/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">7-Zip</a>.</figcaption></figure>
<p>The only files that differ are <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;"><a href="https://www.virustotal.com/gui/file/b1f9b450b97320de54f2450ace151b4f16444dc871f5e89487d52d862ce13cc2" target="_blank" rel="noopener">1.log</a></span>, which contains Base64-encoded text for the PowerShell stealer, and <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;"><a href="https://www.virustotal.com/gui/file/12a00489c8c646e2f558778491751dec9fe6ff1339f7705866f0d7a97123055e" target="_blank" rel="noopener">2.log</a></span>, which contains Base64-encoded text for the keylogger module. The PowerShell stealer is an older version that uses the system’s BIOS serial number instead of the UUID, among other minor differences. The keylogger module is also an older version that uses the BIOS serial number.</p>
<h2><a id="post-143320-_ki9yw764k48k"></a>Conclusion</h2>
<p>Since it first emerged in 2019, the KimJongRAT stealer has evolved, adapting to the changing cybersecurity landscape. Our <a href="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/babyshark-malware-part-two-attacks-continue-using-kimjongrat-and-pcrat/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">previous article</a> highlighted the older variants of this malicious tool, and this article delves deeper into its latest incarnations. One variant uses a PE file, and another is a PowerShell implementation. This adaptability not only showcases the persistent threat posed by such malware but also underscores its developers' commitment to updating and expanding its capabilities.</p>
<p>This new analysis reveals the PowerShell variant's special focus on cryptocurrency, as it searches for an extensive list of browser wallet extensions.</p>
<p>The continued development and deployment of KimJongRAT, featuring changing techniques such as using a legitimate CDN server to disguise its distribution, demonstrates a clear and ongoing threat. Our comprehensive examination of these new variants provides crucial insights into their operation, aiding in the ongoing efforts to detect, neutralize and mitigate their effects.</p>
<p>Palo Alto Networks customers are better protected from the threats described in this article in the following ways:</p>
<ul>
<li>The <a href="https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/wildfire" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Advanced WildFire</a> machine-learning models and analysis techniques have been reviewed and updated in light of the IoCs shared in this research</li>
<li><a href="https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/advanced-url-filtering/administration" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Advanced URL Filtering</a> and <a href="https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/dns-security" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Advanced DNS Security</a> identify known URLs and domains associated with this activity as malicious</li>
<li><a href="https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/advanced-threat-prevention/administration" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Advanced Threat Prevention</a> has an inbuilt machine learning-based detection that can detect exploits in real time.</li>
<li><a href="https://docs-cortex.paloaltonetworks.com/p/XDR" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Cortex XDR</a> and <a href="https://docs-cortex.paloaltonetworks.com/p/XSIAM" target="_blank" rel="noopener">XSIAM</a> are designed to prevent the execution of known malicious malware, and also prevent the execution of unknown malware using Behavioral Threat Protection and machine learning based on the Local Analysis module.</li>
</ul>
<p>If you think you may have been compromised or have an urgent matter, get in touch with the <a href="https://start.paloaltonetworks.com/contact-unit42.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Unit 42 Incident Response team</a> or call:</p>
<ul>
<li>North America: Toll Free: +1 (866) 486-4842 (866.4.UNIT42)</li>
<li>UK: +44.20.3743.3660</li>
<li>Europe and Middle East: +31.20.299.3130</li>

<li>India: 00080005045107</li>
</ul>

CTA members use this intelligence to rapidly deploy protections to their customers and to systematically disrupt malicious cyber actors. Learn more about the <a href="https://www.cyberthreatalliance.org" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Cyber Threat Alliance</a>.</p>

(function($) {
	// Migrated from the unit42-v5 + Modifications
	var subscribeSuccess = false;
	var email = document.getElementById('newsletter-email');
	var subscription_form = document.getElementById('unit42footerSubscription_form');
	var subscription_form_button = document.getElementById('unit42footerSubscription_form_button');
	window.captchaComplete = function() {
		subscribeSuccess = true;
		if ($(mail).val() != '' && isEmail($(mail).val())) {
			$(subscription_form_button).removeClass('is-disabled');
		}
		setTimeout(function() {
			$(email).focus();
			$('.g-recaptcha iframe').attr('tabindex', '-1');
		}, 100)
	}
	window.captchaExpires = function() {
		subscribeSuccess = false;
		$(subscription_form_button).addClass('is-disabled', true);
	} 
	$(subscription_form).submit(function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		e.stopImmediatePropagation();
		updateEmailMask();
		var success = true;
		var form = $(this);
		var mail = form.find('input[name="Email"]');
		
		if (mail.val() === '') {
			mail.addClass('has-error');
			showError(1);
			success = false;	
		}  else if (!isEmail(mail.val())){
			showError(2);
			success = false;
		}
		else {
			mail.removeClass('has-error');
			$('.error-mail').addClass('d-none');
		}

		if (!subscribeSuccess) {
			$('.error-recaptcha').removeClass('d-none');
		} else {
			$('.error-recaptcha').addClass('d-none');
		}

		if (success && subscribeSuccess) {
			$.ajax({
				type: 'POST',
				url: form.attr('action'),
				data: form.serialize(),
				beforeSend: function() {
                 form.find('button').addClass('is-loading');
    			},
				success: function(msg) {
					form.find('.form-success-message').html('<p class="success-message">You have been successfully subscribed</p>');
					form.find('button').removeClass('is-loading');
					$(email).val('');
					clearError();
				},
				error: function(jqXHR, textStatus, errorThrown) {
					$(subscription_form_button).addClass('is-disabled', true);
					form.find('button').removeClass('is-loading');
					
				}
			});
		}
		return false;
	});
	function showError(error_type){
		if(error_type == 1) {
			$('.error-mail').text("Please enter the email address.").addClass('error-show');
			$(subscription_form_button).addClass('is-disabled');
		} else if(error_type == 2){
			$('.error-mail').text("Please provide a valid e-mail address.").addClass('error-show');
			$(subscription_form_button).addClass('is-disabled');
		}	
		$(subscription_form_button).removeClass('is-loading');
	}
	function clearError(){
		$('.error-mail').text("").removeClass('error-show');;
		$(subscription_form_button).removeClass('is-loading');
		$(subscription_form_button).removeClass('is-disabled');
	}
	
	$(email).on('input', function (event) { 
		var email = $(this).val();
		if (isEmail(email) ) {			
			clearError();
		} else if(email == ""){
			clearError();
		} else{
			showError(2);			  
		}
    });

	function isEmail(email) {
		var re = /^(([^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+(\.[^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+)*)|(".+"))@((\[[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\])|(([a-zA-Z\-0-9]+\.)+[a-zA-Z]{2,}))$/;
		return re.test(String(email).toLowerCase());
	}
	
	var captcha_loaded = false;
         if(!captcha_loaded){
            // recaptcha on foucs call
            $(document).on('change paste keyup', '#newsletter-email', function () {
               if($('.g-recaptcha').hasClass('d-none')){
                $('.g-recaptcha').removeClass('d-none');
               }
               if(!captcha_loaded ){
                  captcha_loaded  = true;
                  // trigger loading api.js (recaptcha.js) script
                  var head = document.getElementsByTagName('head')[0];
                  var script = document.createElement('script');
                  script.type = 'text/javascript';
                  script.src = 'https://www.google.com/recaptcha/api.js?hl=en_US';
                  head.appendChild(script);
               }
            });
        }
	
	function updateEmailMask() {
		var email = $("#unit42footerSubscription_form input[name='Email']").val();
		if (email && email.trim() != '') {
			var maskedEmail = maskEmailAddress(email);
			$("#unit42footerSubscription_form input[name='emailFormMask']").val(maskedEmail);
		}
	}

	function maskEmailAddress (emailAddress) {
		function mask(str) {
			var strLen = str.length;
			if (strLen > 4) {
				return str.substr(0, 1) + str.substr(1, strLen - 1).replace(/\w/g, '*') + str.substr(-1,1);
			}
			return str.replace(/\w/g, '*');
		}
		return emailAddress.replace(/([\w.]+)@([\w.]+)(\.[\w.]+)/g, function (m, p1, p2, p3) {
			return mask(p1) + '@' + mask(p2) + p3;
		});

		return emailAddress;
	}

}(jQuery));
//# sourceMappingURL=main.js.map
	
</script>
<!--  End: Footer subscription form -->

			$(".language-dropdown").toggleClass("expand");

			}
		});
	});

	var isProcessing = false; 
    function alter_ul_post_values(obj,post_id,ul_type){
	
		if (isProcessing)    
		return;  
		isProcessing = true;   
		var like_nonce = jQuery('#_wpnonce').val();
		jQuery(obj).find("span").html("..");
                jQuery.ajax({
                    type: "POST",
                    url: "https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/plugins/like-dislike-counter-for-posts-pages-and-comments/ajax_counter.php",
                    data: "post_id="+post_id+"&up_type="+ul_type+"&ul_nonce="+like_nonce,
                    success: function(msg){
                            jQuery(obj).find("span").html(msg);
                            isProcessing = false; 
                            jQuery(obj).find('svg').children('path').attr('stroke','#0050FF');
                            jQuery(obj).removeClass('idc_ul_cont_not_liked idc_ul_cont_not_liked_inner');
                    }
 		});
	}

function loadScript(url, defer){
    var script1 = document.createElement('script');
    script1.setAttribute('type', 'text/javascript');
    script1.setAttribute('src',url);
    if(defer == true){
        script1.setAttribute('defer','defer');
    }
    document.head.appendChild(script1);
}
function loadScript1(url, callback){

    var script = document.createElement("script")
    script.type = "text/javascript";
    if (script.readyState){  //IE
        script.onreadystatechange = function(){
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" || script.readyState == "complete"){
                script.onreadystatechange = null;
                callback();
            }
        };
    } else {  //Others
        script.onload = function(){
            callback();
        };
    }
    script.src = url;
    document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
}
if(referer == "CloudCortex" || referer == "Prisma" || referer == "Cortex" || referer == "Sase" || referer == "Unit" || referer == "Ngfw"){

    }, 3000);
	}
}

document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", function() {
  // Find all the forms on the page
  var forms = document.getElementsByTagName("form");

  // Loop through each form
  for (var i = 0; i < forms.length; i++) {
    var form = forms[i];

    // Check if the hidden input field already exists
    var requestInput = form.querySelector("input[name='web_unit42_req_id']");
    if (!requestInput) {
      // Create a hidden input element if it doesn't exist
      requestInput = document.createElement("input");
      requestInput.type = "hidden";
      requestInput.name = "web_unit42_req_id";
      requestInput.id = "web_unit42_req_id";

      // Append the hidden field to the form
      form.appendChild(requestInput);
    }
  }
});

// Assign the onCheqResponse function to the window object to handle events from any form
window.onCheqResponse = function(encryptedMessage, requestID) {
  // Find all the forms on the page
  var forms = document.getElementsByTagName("form");

  for (var i = 0; i < forms.length; i++) {
    var form = forms[i];
    var requestInput = form.querySelector("input[name='web_unit42_req_id']");
    if (requestInput) {
      requestInput.value = requestID;
    }
  }
};
